The Pre-Eternity of All Divine Attributes
Sanusi proves the pre-eternity of all divine attributes by showing their contingency would entail God's contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the pre-eternity of all divine attributes is a necessary conclusion from God's own pre-eternity, and how Sanusi proves this with two linked arguments.

Core Idea
If a single attribute of God were originated, God Himself would be originated.

Sanusi now turns to a crucial implication of the attributes he has just established. If God's attributes are real, they must share in His pre-eternity. This short but dense passage contains two linked proofs that any originated attribute would force God's own contingency, which is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thesis
The passage opens with the claim: all attributes must be eternal. Pause to appreciate what is being proven.
2
Trace the first argument
Follow the conditional: if an attribute were originated, then God would either be without it or with its originated opposite—both impossible for the Eternal.
Notice the use of 'طريان عدم' as proof of origination.
3
Trace the second argument
The second argument is more direct: an originated attribute would entail God's own origination. Understand why that is a contradiction.
This second argument is a concise summary of the first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في قدم صفات اللہ تعالى
ثم نقولُ : يتعيَّنُ أنْ تكونَ هذه الصفات كلُّها قديمةً ؛ إذ لو كانَ شيءٌ منها حادثاً لَلزِمَ ألا يعرى عنه أو عن الاتصاف بضده الحادثِ (۱) ، ودليل حدوثِهِ : طريان عدمِهِ ؛ لما علمْتَ مِن استحالة عدم القديم ، وما لا تُتحقَّقُ ذاتُهُ بدونِ حادث .. يلزمُ حدوثه ضرورةً ، وقد تقدَّمَ مثلُ ذلك في الاستدلال على حدوث العالم (۲)
لمَّا فرغَ مِنْ إقامةِ البرهان على ثبوتِ الصفاتِ.. شرع في إثباتِ
أحكام واجبة لها
فمن ذلك : القدم
.
ودليل وجوبِهِ لكلِّ ما يَتَصفُ بهِ تعالى : أَنَّهُ لو كانَ شَيءٌ مِنْ صفاتِهِ جل وعلا حادثاً .. لَلزِمَ حدوثه ، والتالي باطل ؛ لما عرفتَ مِنْ وجوب قدمِهِ تعالى ، فالمقدم مثلُهُ
Chapter on the pre-eternity of God's attributes.
Then we say: It is necessary that all these attributes be eternal; for if any of them were originated, then it would be impossible that [the Essence] be devoid of it or of being characterized by its originated opposite (1). The proof of its origination is the occurrence of its non-existence; because you know the impossibility of non-existence of the eternal. And whatever its essence is not realized without an originated thing, its origination is necessary. An example like that has preceded in proving the origination of the world (2).
When he finished establishing the proof for the existence of the attributes, he began to prove necessary rulings for them.
From that is: pre-eternity.
The proof of its necessity for every attribute with which He is described: That if any of His attributes, mighty and sublime, were originated, then His origination would be necessary. The consequent is false, because you know the necessary pre-eternity of God; so the antecedent is likewise [false].
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a formal proof (burhan) for the pre-eternity (qidam) of God's attributes. The author begins with the conclusion: all attributes must be eternal. He provides two arguments. First: if an attribute were originated, then God would either be characterized by it (which is impossible because it would not be His attribute at all if originated and then later attached? Actually, the argument is that if originated, it would either be present or its opposite present, both originated, implying change in God which is impossible. The proof of its origination is that it could cease to exist, but the eternal cannot cease. Second: if any attribute were originated, then God's essence would not be realized without that originated attribute, implying God's own origination. Since God is eternal, the attribute must be eternal. The author then notes that after proving the existence of attributes, we now prove necessary properties like pre-eternity. The specific proof for pre-eternity of each attribute is that if it were originated, then God would be originated (because He is always described by it or its opposite), which is false; therefore the attribute is not originated.

صفات
حادث
قديم
دليل
طريان عدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only some divine attributes (like knowledge and power) are eternal, while others (like will or speech) may be originated.
Correction: Sanusi argues that all attributes that are truly essential to God must be eternal. The proof applies to any attribute that God is described with, without exception.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would be the consequence if any of God's attributes were originated?
A) God would have an eternal opposite.
B) God Himself would be originated.
C) The attribute would be both eternal and originated.
D) The attribute would be impossible.

Key Takeaway
The pre-eternity of God necessitates the pre-eternity of all His essential attributes; any originated attribute would entail God's own origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Proof that All Divine Attributes Are Pre-Eternal
Sanusi proves the pre-eternity of all divine attributes through a conditional argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that all of God's attributes must be pre-eternal and why no attribute can be temporal.

Core Idea
If even one attribute of God were temporal, God Himself would be temporal — which is impossible.

This passage from Sanusi's creedal work establishes a foundational principle about God's attributes. After proving that God has attributes, the author now demonstrates that these attributes must be pre-eternal (qadim) like God's essence. The argument relies on a logical principle: whatever cannot be free from temporal things must itself be temporal. Read on to see how Sanusi applies this principle to prove the eternity of all divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic text and its literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you start analyzing.
Notice the dense logical structure; take your time.
2
Identify the main claim and the conditional structure
The passage begins with the claim that all attributes must be pre-eternal. Then it presents a conditional: if any attribute were temporal, then God would be temporal. Understand this 'if-then' structure.
The proof is essentially a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Understand the principle of entailment
Sanusi explains why temporality of an attribute forces temporality of the essence: because the essence cannot be free from that attribute or its opposite. If the attribute is temporal, the essence is never free from temporal accidents, so the essence must be temporal.
This is the key logical move.
4
Reflect on the conclusion and its implications
Since God is necessarily pre-eternal, the consequence is false, so the antecedent (that an attribute is temporal) must be false. Thus all attributes are pre-eternal.
Sanusi also connects this to his earlier proof of the world's temporality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في قدم صفات اللہ تعالى ثم نقولُ : يتعيَّنُ أنْ تكونَ هذه الصفات كلُّها قديمةً ; إذ لو كانَ شيءٌ منها حادثاً لَلزِمَ ألا يعرى عنه أو عن الاتصاف بضده الحادثِ ، ودليل حدوثِهِ : طريان عدمِهِ ; لما علمْتَ مِن استحالة عدم القديم ، وما لا تُتحقَّقُ ذاتُهُ بدونِ حادث .. يلزمُ حدوثه ضرورةً ، وقد تقدَّمَ مثلُ ذلك في الاستدلال على حدوث العالم لمَّا فرغَ مِنْ إقامةِ البرهان على ثبوتِ الصفاتِ.. شرع في إثباتِ أحكام واجبة لها فمن ذلك : القدوم . ودليل وجوبِهِ لكلِّ ما يَتَصفُ بهِ تعالى : أَنَّهُ لو كانَ شَيءٌ مِنْ صفاتِهِ جل وعلا حادثاً .. لَلزِمَ حدوثه ، والتالي باطل ; لما عرفتَ مِنْ وجوب قدمِهِ تعالى ، فالمقدم مثلُهُ وبيان الملازمة : ما أشرنا إليه في أصل العقيدة مِنْ أنَّه لو كان شيء مِنْ صفاتِهِ تعالى حادثاً .. لَلزِمَ ألا يعرى عنه أو عن ضدّه الحادثِ ; لما عرفت - فيما مضى ، وسنعيد أيضاً برهانه فيما بعد - مِنْ أَنَّ القابل للشيء لا يخلو عنه أو عن ضدّهِ ، وما لا يعـرى عـن الحـوادث لا يسبقها ، وما لا يسبقها كانَ حادثاً مثلها ، وهو معنى قولي : ( وما لا تتحقق ذاته بدون حادث .. يلزم حدوثه ضرورةً ) أي : ما لا يمكن مفارقة ذاتِهِ للحوادثِ .. يلزمُ حدوثه ضرورة ; إذ لو كان هو قديماً ووصفه اللازم له حادثاً .. لكان مفارقاً لوصفه اللازم ، كيف وقد تُحقَّقَ أَنَّهُ لا يفارقه ؟!
Chapter on the pre-eternity of God's attributes. Then we say: It is necessarily the case that all these attributes are pre-eternal; for if any of them were temporal, it would necessarily imply that He is not free from it or from being characterized by its temporal opposite. And the proof of its temporality is the occurrence of its non-existence; because you know the impossibility of the non-existence of the pre-eternal. And that whose essence is not realized without a temporal thing necessarily implies its temporality. And the like of that has already preceded in the proof of the temporality of the world. When he finished establishing proof of the existence of the attributes, he began to prove necessary rulings for them, among which is pre-eternity. And the proof of its necessity for everything by which He, exalted, is characterized: that if any of His attributes, glory be to Him and exalted, were temporal, then His temporality would be necessary; and the consequent is false because you have known the necessity of His pre-eternity, so the antecedent is likewise. And the explanation of the entailment: what we pointed to in the foundation of the creed: that if something of His attributes, exalted, were temporal, then it would necessarily follow that He is not free from it or from its temporal opposite; because you have known – from what has preceded, and we will repeat its proof later – that that which is receptive to a thing is not free from it or from its opposite; and that which is not free from temporal things does not precede them; and that which does not precede them is temporal like them. And that is the meaning of my statement: 'And that whose essence is not realized without a temporal thing necessarily implies its temporality,' i.e., that whose essence cannot be free from temporal things necessarily implies its temporality; for if it were pre-eternal and its necessary description were temporal, it would be separate from its necessary description, but how can it be when it has been realized that it is not separate from it?!
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the pre-eternity (qidam) of all God's attributes. The author begins by stating the claim: all attributes must be pre-eternal. He then gives a conditional proof: if any attribute were temporal (hadith), the essence would be inseparable from it or from its temporal opposite. This is based on the principle that whatever receives something cannot be free from it or its opposite. Thus, the essence would always be accompanied by temporal things, which would imply that the essence is itself temporal, because that which does not precede temporal things is temporal. The author also gives a simpler version: if an attribute were temporal, then God would be temporal, which is false since God is necessarily pre-eternal. He then elaborates the entailment (mulazama): if something is receptive to a thing, it must be either with that thing or its opposite; hence if the attribute is temporal, the essence is never free from temporal accidents, so the essence is temporal. He concludes with a rhetorical question: if God is pre-eternal and His necessary attribute is temporal, then He would be separate from that necessary attribute, but it has been established that He is not separate from it.

Key Terms
قدم (qidam)
حادث (hadith)
ضد (did)
ملازمة (mulazama)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that some attributes could be temporal while God is eternal, as long as the essence itself remains eternal.
Correction: Sanusi shows that if any attribute were temporal, God's essence would be inseparable from temporal accidents, making the essence itself temporal. Since God is necessarily pre-eternal, no attribute can be temporal.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what would necessarily follow if any of God's attributes were temporal (hadith)?
A) God's essence would be temporal.
B) The attribute could still be pre-eternal.
C) God would not be affected.
D) The Qur'anic text would be contradicted.

Key Takeaway
All of God's attributes must be pre-eternal because temporality in any attribute would entail temporality in God's essence, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's attributes are eternal and unchanging, does your perception of His mercy toward you change when you sin? How will you remind yourself tomorrow that His mercy is not a reaction to your deeds but an eternal attribute?
?
You learned that even one temporal attribute would make God temporal. Does your daily life reflect a belief that God is absolutely unchanging, or do you sometimes act as if He is affected by time? What concrete habit can you adopt to align your heart with this truth?
?
Imagine standing before God and realizing you lived as if His justice or love could be earned or diminished. How does the pre-eternity of His attributes demand a fundamental shift in your worship and reliance on Him? What will you change starting today?

Objection and Answer on the Pre-Eternity of Attribute Opposites
Sanusi addresses an objection: could the opposite of a temporal attribute be pre-eternal?

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that the opposite of a temporal attribute could be pre-eternal, and why Sanusi argues this is impossible.

Core Idea
If one attribute is temporal, its opposite must also be temporal.

In this passage, Sanusi anticipates a potential criticism to his proof of the creation of attributes. An objector argues that the opposite of a temporal attribute could be pre-eternal, thereby avoiding the necessity of change in the divine essence. Sanusi begins his reply by demonstrating why such a scenario is impossible, although the full argument is cut off at the end of the page.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the flow from the objection to the answer.
The answer is incomplete; note where it cuts off.
2
Identify the objection
The objector's claim is that the opposite of a temporal attribute could be pre-eternal. Find the exact phrasing in the text.
The objector says 'نمنعُ أنَّ ضدَّهُ حادث' (we deny that its opposite is temporal).
3
Understand the answer's beginning
Sanusi responds by stating that if an attribute is temporal, its opposite must also be temporal. Consider why that would be necessary.
The text ends with 'لما', indicating the argument is unfinished.
4
Reflect on the logical principle
Contraries cannot coexist; if one opposite is temporal, the other cannot be eternal in the same subject. Think about how this applies to God's attributes.
This guards against the idea of a mixed set of eternal and temporal attributes.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قولي : ( ودليل حدوثِهِ : طريانُ عدمِهِ ) فهو جواب عن سؤال مستشعرٍ في قولي : ( للزِمَ ألا يعرى عنه أو عن الاتِّصافِ بضدِّهِ الحادث ) عن وتقريره أنْ يُقالَ : لا نُسلَّمُ أَنَّهُ لو كانَ شيءٌ مِنْ صفاتِهِ تعالى حادثاً يلزم حدوثه ، قولكم : ( إنَّه لا يعرى عنه أو عن ضدّهِ الحادثِ ) نمنعُ أنَّ ضدَّهُ حادث ، بل يجوز أن يكون قديماً ، فحينئذٍ إِنَّما يلزم ألا يعرى ذلك الحادثِ أو عن ضدّهِ القديم ، وذلك لا يستلزم حدوثه ; لأنَّه لم يلزم إذ ذاكَ مِنْ قدمِهِ تعالى وحدوثِ بعض صفاته عروه عن جميع أوصافهِ; لفَرْضِ القدم في بعضها، وهو أضداد تلك الأوصاف الحادثة . وجوابه : أَنَّهُ يلزمُ مِنْ تقديرِ الحدوثِ لصفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ أنْ يكونَ ضدُّها حادثاً ، ويستحيلُ أنْ يكونَ قديماً ; وذلك لأنَّهُ لو كان قديماً لما
As for my statement: 'And the proof of its temporality is the occurrence of its non-existence,' it is an answer to a question sensed in my statement: 'It would necessarily not be free from it or from being characterized by its temporal opposite.' Its formulation is that it is said: We do not grant that if something of His attributes, exalted, were temporal, its temporality would be necessary. As for your statement: 'It is not free from it or from its temporal opposite,' we deny that its opposite is temporal; rather, it is possible that it is pre-eternal. In that case, it would only follow that it is not free from that temporal thing or from its pre-eternal opposite, and that does not necessitate its temporality, because then it does not follow from His pre-eternity and the temporality of some of His attributes that He is free from all His attributes, due to the assumption of pre-eternity in some of them, namely the opposites of those temporal attributes. And its answer: That from the estimation of temporality for one of His attributes, it follows that its opposite is temporal, and it is impossible for it to be pre-eternal; because if it were pre-eternal, it would...
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its partial answer. The author anticipates a criticism: if one of God's attributes were temporal, why must His essence be temporal? The objector says: We do not grant the claim that the opposite of the temporal attribute is necessarily temporal; it could be pre-eternal. If that opposite is pre-eternal, then the essence might always be characterized by the pre-eternal opposite, so it would not be inseparable from temporal things alone. Thus, the temporality of the essence does not necessarily follow. The author's answer begins: If we assume temporality for one attribute, its opposite must also be temporal, because if the opposite were pre-eternal, then... (the text cuts off). The argument likely continues to show that a pre-eternal opposite cannot coexist with a temporal attribute in the same subject without contradiction. This answer guards against the idea that God could have a mix of temporal and eternal attributes.

Correction: Sanusi argues that if one attribute is temporal, its opposite must also be temporal because they are contraries.

C) God cannot have attributes at all.
D) The Qur'an denies pre-eternity of attributes.

Key Takeaway
If one divine attribute is temporal, its opposite must also be temporal.

Refuting the Objection of Emptiness from Both Quality and Opposite
Sanusi refutes the objection that a subject could be timeless while empty of all temporal qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's refutation of the objection that a subject could be timeless while empty of both a quality and its opposite, and why the capacity for attributes must be intrinsic to avoid circularity or infinite regress.

Core Idea
Capacity for attributes must be intrinsic, or else reason spins into circles.

Sanusi presents a crucial objection to the argument that what receives temporal attributes must itself be temporal. The objection suggests that a subject could be eternally empty of both a quality and its opposite, then later acquire them. Sanusi's response shows that the very capacity to receive attributes must be intrinsic to the subject; otherwise, an infinite regress of capacities would destroy the argument. This passage deepens our understanding of divine attributes and the logic of temporality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the objection
The passage presents an objection: a subject could be timeless while being devoid of both a quality and its opposite, then later acquire them. Find where this objection is stated and understand its challenge to the main argument.
The objection is framed as 'if you say...'
3
Understand the answer: capacity is intrinsic
Sanusi's answer is that the capacity (qabul) for attributes must be intrinsic (nafsi) to the subject. If it were not, it would lead to circularity or infinite regress. Grasp why intrinsic capacity is necessary.
4
See the proof by regression
Sanusi provides a proof: if capacity were accidental, it would require a prior capacity, leading to dawr (circularity) or tasalsul (infinite regress). Follow the logical steps to see why this is impossible.
This proof is essential for defending divine eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تأكيد أن ما لازم الحادث فهو حادث فإن قلت: إنما يتم ذلك إذا وجب أن القابل للشيء لا يخلو عنه أو عن ضده، ولم لا يقال بجواز خلوه عنهما معا، ثم يطرأ الاتصاف بهما، فتتحقق ذاته دونهما فلا يلزم الحدوث؟ فالجواب: أنه لو خلا عنهما مع قبوله لهما لجاز أن يخلو عن جميع ما يقبله من الصفات؛ إذ القبول لا يختلف؛ لأنه نفسي، وإلا لزم الدور أو التسلسل. وخلو القابل عن جميع الحادث محال مطلقا؛ لوجوب اتصافه بالأكوان ضرورة، وفي القديم؛ لوجوب اتصافه بما دل عليه فعله كالعلم والقدرة والإرادة، ولو فرضت حادثة للزم الدور أو التسلسل لتوقف إحداثها عليها. هذا اعتراض آخر على الملازمة في قولنا: (لو كان شيء من صفاته تعالى حادثا للزم حدوثه). وتقريره أن يقال: لا نسلم ملزومية حدوث الصفات لحدوث الموصوف، قولكم: (لأنه لا يعرى عنها أو عن أضدادها الحادثة) دعوى، قولكم في بيانها: (لأن الموصوف بها قابل لها، والقابل للشيء لا يخلو عنه أو عن ضده) غير مسلم، وما المانع أن يقال بجواز خلو القابل للصفة عنها وعن ضدها، ويكون قديما عاريا عن جميع ما يقبله من الصفات، ثم يتصف بها أو ببعضها فيما لا يزال؟ فلا يلزم حينئذ من اتصافه بالحوادث حدوثه؛ لما ذكرنا من صحة مفارقته لجميعها. وجوابه: أن قبول كل ذات لما تتصف به من الصفات لا يكون أبدا إلا نفسيا لتلك الذات؛ أي يجب لها ذلك القبول ما دامت الذات غير معلل بمعنى. والدليل عليه: أنه لو لم يكن القبول نفسيا للذات، بل كان يطرأ عليها بعد أن لم يكن لتوقف في طروئه على الذات على قبولها إياه فيكون قبول هذا القبول صفة للذات طارئا أيضا عليها، فيحتاج في طروه على الذات إلى قبولها أيضا له، فإن كان القبول الأول لزم الدور، وإن كان قبولا آخر غيره نقلنا الكلام إليه أيضا ولزم التسلسل. وإلى هذا أشرت بقولي: (لأنه نفسي، وإلا لزم الدور أو التسلسل). وإذا ثبت أن القبول نفسي للذات لزم أن تكون نسبة...
Confirmation that whatever is inseparable from a temporal thing is itself temporal. If you say: This only follows if it is necessary that the recipient of a thing is not devoid of it or its opposite. Why can it not be said that it is possible for it to be devoid of both together, then the qualification by them occurs as an accident, so its essence is realized without them, and temporality does not follow? The answer: If it were devoid of both while having the capacity for them, then it would be possible for it to be devoid of all the attributes it receives; because the capacity does not differ; for it is intrinsic, otherwise circularity or infinite regress would follow. And the recipient being devoid of all temporal things is absolutely impossible; because of the necessity of its being qualified by spatial accidents necessarily, and in the Eternal, because of the necessity of His being qualified by what His act indicates, such as knowledge, power, and will, and if they were supposed temporal, circularity or infinite regress would follow due to the dependence of their origination on them. This is another objection to the implication in our statement: (If any of His attributes were temporal, then His temporality would follow). Its restatement: It is said: We do not grant that the temporality of the attributes necessitates the temporality of the qualified. Your statement: (Because it is not free from them or from their temporal opposites) is a claim. Your statement in its explanation: (Because the qualified has capacity for them, and the recipient of a thing is not devoid of it or its opposite) is not granted. What prevents it from being said that it is permissible for the recipient of the attribute to be devoid of it and its opposite, and be eternal, bare of all the temporal attributes it receives, then become qualified by them or some of them in what will be? Then it would not follow from its being qualified by temporal things that it is temporal; because of what we mentioned of the validity of its separation from all of them. Its answer: That the capacity of every essence for the attributes it is qualified by is never except intrinsic to that essence; i.e., that capacity is necessary for it as long as the essence is not caused by a meaning. The proof for it is: If the capacity were not intrinsic to the essence, but rather it occurred to it after not having been, then its occurrence to the essence would depend on the essence's acceptance of it, so the acceptance of this capacity would be an attribute of the essence also occurring to it, so it would need, in its occurrence to the essence, also its acceptance of it. If it were the first capacity, circularity would follow; if it were another capacity different from it, we would transfer the argument to it also and infinite regress would follow. And to this I alluded with my statement: (Because it is intrinsic, otherwise circularity or infinite regress would follow). And if it is established that the capacity is intrinsic to the essence, then it follows that the relationship...
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a detailed objection-and-answer within the argument that any subject receiving temporal attributes must itself be temporal. The objection claims that a subject could be timeless while being devoid of both a quality and its opposite, then later acquire them. The answer refutes this by showing that the capacity (qabul) for attributes must be intrinsic (nafsi) to the subject. If it were not intrinsic, it would itself require a prior capacity, leading to circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul). The author first restates the objection more fully, then provides the definitive answer: the capacity is intrinsic, proven by the impossibility of an accidental capacity because that would require an endless chain of capacities. The argument is foundational for defending divine eternity against the claim that God's attributes necessitate His temporality.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A subject can be free of both a quality and its opposite without any intrinsic disposition, remaining eternal while later acquiring qualities.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the very capacity for qualities is intrinsic to the subject; otherwise, an infinite regress results. Thus the subject cannot be truly bare of all capacity.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what would happen if the capacity (qabul) for attributes were not intrinsic to the subject?
A) The subject would become temporal.
B) Circularity or infinite regress would follow.
C) The subject would be free of all attributes.
D) The attributes would be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The capacity for attributes must be intrinsic to the subject; otherwise, circularity or infinite regress would result, proving that a subject that receives temporal attributes must itself be temporal.

Sanusi argues that if capacity were accidental, an infinite regress would follow. Consider your own understanding of God's attributes: do you ever treat them as if they were added to God's essence rather than being intrinsic? What does that do to your trust in His decrees, and what step will you take to correct that assumption starting today?

The Objection: Attributes Can Be Acquired Later
Sanusi presents the opponent's objection that attributes can be acquired after being absent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponent's objection that a subject can be eternal and bare of all attributes, then acquire them later, and why this challenges the argument for the creation of the subject.

Core Idea
The opponent claims a subject can be free of all attributes in pre-eternity and acquire them later.

In this lesson, Sanusi presents an objection from an unnamed opponent. The opponent rejects the necessary connection between the subject being created and its attributes being created. They propose an alternative: a subject can be eternal and bare of all attributes, then later become qualified by them. Understanding this objection is crucial for following the subsequent refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the opponent's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the structure: rejection, challenge, alternative scenario, conclusion.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent claims that a subject can be eternal (قديم) and stripped of all created attributes, and then later become qualified by them. Find the sentence that states this.
Look for 'وما المانع أن يقال بجواز خلو القابل للصفة عنها وعن ضدها'
3
Understand the key terms
Review the Arabic terms: ملزومية (entailment), حدوث (creation/occurrence), موصوف (described subject), قابل (receptive), صفة (attribute), قديم (eternal), حوادث (created things).
These terms are central to the argument.
4
Note the footnote clarification
The footnote explains the word غير معلل (unqualified) and the meaning of دام and بمعنى. This clarifies the opponent's stance on the attribute's relation to the essence.
This is a technical note on kalām terminology.
5
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: If the opponent's scenario is possible, what happens to the proof that the subject must be created? This objection is a key challenge in the debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتقريره أن يُقالَ : لا نُسلَّمُ ملزومية حدوث الصفاتِ لحدوثِ الموصوف ، قولكم : ( لأنَّه لا يعرى عنها أو عن أضدادها الحادثة ) دعوى ، قولكم في بيانها : ( لأنَّ الموصوف بها قابل لها ، والقابل للشيء لا يخلو عنه أو عن ضدّهِ ( غيرُ مُسلَّم ، وما المانعُ أنْ يُقالَ بجواز خلوّ القابل للصفة عنها وعن ضدّها ، ويكون قديماً عارياً أوصافه الحادثة التي يقبلها ، ثم يتّصف بها أو ببعضها الأزلِ عن جميعِ فيما لا يزالُ ؟ فَلا يلزمُ حِينَئِذٍ مِن اتصافِهِ بالحوادثِ حدوثه ؛ لما ذكرنا مِنْ صحة مفارقتِهِ لجميعها (۱) قلها : ( غير معلَّل ( حال من ( القبول ) ، و ( دام ) في ( ما دامت ) هنا تامة ، وقوله : ( بمعنى ) أي : قائم بالذات ، احترز بذلك عن الحال المعنوية ؛ فإنها تجب للذات مع كونها معللة بمعنى . مفاد « حامدي » ( ص ٢٥٣ ) .
And its exposition: It is said: We do not accept that the creation of attributes is entailed by the creation of the described [subject]. Your statement: (Because it cannot be free of them or of their created opposites) is a claim. Your statement in its explanation: (Because the described is receptive to them, and the receptive to a thing cannot be free of it or its opposite) is not accepted. And what prevents saying that it is permissible for the receptive to an attribute to be free of it and its opposite, and that it is eternal, stripped of the created attributes that it accepts, then it becomes qualified by them or by some of them in what [will be] thereafter? So then, from its being qualified by created [attributes], its creation does not follow; because of what we mentioned of the validity of its separating from all of them. (1) Say: (غير معلَّل [unqualified] is a state from القبول [acceptance], and دام in ما دامت here is complete, and his statement بمعنى means: subsisting in the essence, and he thereby excludes the literal state [الحال المعنوية]; for they are necessary for the essence despite being qualified by a meaning. The purport of Hamidi (p. 253).
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the argument that attributes must be created if the subject is created. The opponent argues: they do not accept that the creation of attributes is entailed by the creation of the subject. They challenge the claim that a subject cannot be free of an attribute or its opposite, saying this is not accepted. They propose instead that it is possible for a receptive entity to be devoid of both the attribute and its opposite, and for it to be eternal (قَديم) while being stripped of all created attributes that it accepts, and then later become qualified by them. Thus, acquiring attributes later does not entail that the subject itself is created. The footnote clarifies some terms: 'غير معلَّل' is a state of the acceptance, and the word 'دام' is complete, and 'بمعنى' means subsisting in the essence, distinguishing from the literal state (الحال المعنوية).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the opponent's claim is that God could be devoid of attributes, but this objection is about contingent beings, as a step in the argument.
Correction: The objection is part of a broader argument about the nature of attributes; the 'subject' here is a hypothetical receptive entity, not necessarily God.

Checkpoint
What does the opponent claim about the relationship between a subject and its attributes?
A) The subject must always have attributes.
B) The subject can be free of all attributes in pre-eternity and acquire them later.
C) The subject's attributes are eternal.
D) The subject's creation entails the creation of attributes.

Key Takeaway
The opponent argues that a subject can be eternal and free of all attributes, then acquire them later, so being qualified by created attributes does not imply the subject's creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The opponent asks 'وما المانع' (what prevents saying) - a question that opens up reconsideration of a standard argument. Are you willing to ask 'what prevents' for your own deeply held assumptions, even those about God? What is one assumption you have been too afraid to question? How will you face that fear?
?
The counter-scenario describes an eternal thing that later acquires attributes. In your own spiritual journey, do you treat your character as fixed (like an eternal unchangeable thing) or as something that can acquire new attributes over time? What one attribute do you need to acquire, and what is stopping you from seeking it starting today?

Why Acceptance of Attributes Is Essential
Sanusi proves that acceptance of attributes is essential to the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the acceptance of attributes is considered an essential (nafsi) characteristic of the divine essence, and how Sanusi proves this through the avoidance of circularity or infinite regress.

Core Idea
Acceptance of attributes is inherent to the essence, or endless circularity would result.

Sanusi addresses a key objection about how attributes relate to the essence. He argues that the very receptivity (قبول) to attributes must be an intrinsic part of the essence, not something added later. This short passage proves why that must be so, using a powerful logical argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Pay attention to the key terms and the logical flow.
2
Identify the claim
Find the statement that acceptance is essential (nafsiyyan) to the essence. Note that Sanusi says it is 'never except essential'.
The term 'nafsi' is crucial here.
3
Understand the proof structure
Notice the conditional proof: if acceptance were not essential, then it would occur later, leading to a dilemma of circularity or infinite regress. Trace both branches.
The proof is by contradiction.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Why does this matter for divine attributes? If acceptance were not essential, the essence could not properly be the subject of attributes. This grounds the possibility of divine attributes in a necessary feature of the essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوابُهُ : أَنَّ قَبول كلِّ ذاتِ لما تتَصفُ  ِبهِ مِنَ الصفاتِ لا يكونُ أبداً إلا نفسيّاً لتلك الذاتِ ؛ أي : يجب لها ذلكَ القَبولُ ما دامَتِ الذاتُ غير مُعلَّل بمعنى (١) . والدليل عليهِ : أَنَّهُ لو لم يكن القبولُ نفسياً للذاتِ ، بل كان يطرأ عليها بعد أنْ لم يكن .. لتوقف في طروِّهِ على الذاتِ على قبولِها إِيَّاهُ فيكونُ قَبولُ هذا القبولِ صفة للذاتِ طارئاً أيضاً عليها ، فيحتاج في طروه على الذاتِ إلى قبولها أيضاً لهُ ، فإنْ كانَ القَبول الأَوَّلَ لزمَ الدورُ . وإن كان قبولاً آخرَ غيرَهُ .. نقلنا الكلام إليه أيضاً ، ولزم التسلسل . • وإلى هذا أشرتُ بقولي : ( لأنَّه نفسي ، وإلا لزم الدورُ أَوِ التسلسل )
And his answer: That the acceptance of every essence for what it is qualified by of the attributes is never except essential (nafsiyyan) to that essence; i.e., that acceptance is necessary for it as long as the essence exists, not caused by a meaning (bi-maʿnā). The proof for it: That if the acceptance were not essential to the essence, but rather it occurred to it after it had not been... then the occurrence of that acceptance would depend on the essence's acceptance of it, so the acceptance of this acceptance would be an attribute occurring to the essence as well, and it would need for its occurrence to the essence its acceptance also of it. If it were the first acceptance, then circularity follows. If it were another acceptance other than it, then we transfer the speech to it also, and infinite regress follows. • And to this I alluded by my statement: (Because it is essential, otherwise circularity or infinite regress would follow).
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage gives Sanusi's answer to the objection. He argues that the acceptance (قبول) of attributes by an essence is always 'essential' (نفسي) to that essence, meaning the essence necessarily has this receptivity as long as it exists, and it is not caused by an external meaning. He then proves this: if the acceptance were not essential but occurred afterward, then its occurrence would itself require a prior acceptance by the essence, leading to either circularity (دور) if it is the same acceptance, or infinite regress (تسلسل) if it is another acceptance. Thus acceptance must be essential. He concludes by referencing his own statement that it is essential, otherwise circularity or regress would occur.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Receptivity to attributes is an acquired quality that the essence gains at the moment of being described.
Correction: Sanusi shows that acceptance must be essential (nafsi) to the essence, meaning it is a necessary, inherent feature, not something acquired later. Otherwise the logic leads to circularity or infinite regress.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi prove about the acceptance of attributes?
A) It is acquired later.
B) It is essential to the essence.
C) It is created.
D) It is optional.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of attributes is an essential (nafsi) attribute of the divine essence; otherwise, the argument falls into circularity or infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

If God's acceptance of attributes were not essential, then He would be incomplete before acquiring them. Do you truly live as if God is complete and perfect in every moment, or do you sometimes act as if He needs something from you?
?
The proof shows that circularity and regress are impossible in God's attributes. Reflect: Is there a circularity in your own heart where you love God only when He gives, rather than loving Him for His eternal and essential perfections? What would it take to break that cycle?

Implications: Essence Cannot Be Devoid of Any Attribute
Sanusi argues that essential acceptance entails the impossibility of being devoid of any attribute, then proves God's attributes are eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the essential acceptance of attributes implies that an essence cannot be devoid of any attribute it accepts, and how this leads to the eternity of all of God's attributes.

Core Idea
If acceptance is essential, lacking any attribute is impossible.

Sanusi now draws out a profound implication: if an essence inherently accepts attributes, it cannot be stripped of any of them. This principle applies to both created beings and God, but with different outcomes. For God, it means every attribute He possesses is eternal, just as His essence is eternal. In this passage, Sanusi builds a rigorous argument from the nature of acceptance to the eternity of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the key premise
The passage begins by establishing that if acceptance is essential (nafsī) to the essence, then the relationship of the essence to all its accepted attributes is identical. This is crucial for the argument.
This premise was established in previous lessons.
2
Follow the logical implication
If the relationship is equal, then either the essence can lack all attributes or none. Since lacking all is impossible (as shown by examples), the essence must possess every attribute it accepts.
Sanusi uses a reductio: if lacking all were possible, then lacking any would be possible, but lacking all is impossible.
3
Examine the two applications
Sanusi applies this to contingent beings (atoms cannot lack accidents) and to God (His acts prove He must have attributes like knowledge and power, so He cannot lack them).
For atoms, we know necessarily that they require accidents; for God, we infer attributes from His actions.
4
Conclude the eternity of attributes
Because God's essence is eternal and cannot lack any attribute, all His attributes must be eternal. If any attribute were created, the essence would be created—impossible.
This is the final conclusion of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت أنَّ القبول نفسي للذاتِ.. لزمَ أنْ تكونَ نسبةُ صفاتها إليها قبولاً واتصافاً نسبةً واحدةً ، فلو جازَ خلوها عن جميع أجناس صفاتها التي تقبلها لجازَ خلوها عن جميع تلك الأجناس المقبولة ضرورة استواء نسبة الجميع إليها ، لكن خلو الذاتِ عن ما تقبلُهُ مِنْ أجناس الصفاتِ محال مطلقاً ؛ أعني : في حق الحادثِ وفي حقِّ القديم، فخلوها عن بعض أجناس صفاتها التي تقبلها محال . أما استحالةُ الخلوّ عنِ الجميع في حق الحادثِ : فلانا نعلم على الضرورة استحالة عرو الجواهر عن جنس الأكوان ؛ وهي الحركة والسكون ، والاجتماع والافتراقُ ، فيجب ألا تعرى عن سائر أجناس الأعراض التي تقبلها . وأما في حق القديمِ جلَّ وعلا : فلانا نعلم قطعاً استحالة عروهِ عمَّا جميع الصفات دلّ عليه فعله ؛ مِنَ العَلمِ والقدرةِ والإرادة والحياة ؛ إذ لو انتفت حقه هذه الصفاتُ لاستحالَ أنْ يُوجِدَ فعلاً مِنْ أفعالِهِ ، فيلزم عدمُ المصنوعاتِ كلّها مع تحقق وجودها ، وهو محال على الضرورة ، وإذا استحال عروه عن هذهِ الصفاتِ لزم استحالة عروه عن سائر الصفاتِ التي يقبلُها ؛ لما عرفتَ مِنْ وجوب استواء نسبة المقبولة إلى الذاتِ القابلة لها ، وإذا ثبت التلازم بينَ وجودِ ذاتِهِ تعالى وبين جميع صفاتِهِ التي ينصفُ بها .. لزم أن تكون كلها قديمةً ؛ إذ لو كانَ شيء منها حادثاً والفَرْضُ أَنَّهُ لا يمكنُ أنْ يعرى عن صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ. . لَلزِمَ أنْ يكونَ وجود ذاتِهِ حادثاً ، لكن الحدوث على ذاتِهِ مستحيل ؛ لما عرفتَ مِنْ وجوبِ قدمِهِ ، فَفَرْضُ الحدوثِ في صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ مستحيل
And when it is established that the acceptance is essential (nafsī) to the essence... then it necessarily follows that the relationship of its attributes to it, in terms of acceptance and qualification, is one relationship. So if it were possible for it to be free of all kinds of attributes that it accepts, then it would be possible for it to be free of all those accepted kinds because of the necessity of the equality of the relationship of all to it. But the essence's being free of what it accepts from the kinds of attributes is absolutely impossible; meaning: in the case of the created (hadith) and in the case of the Eternal (qadīm). So its being free of some kinds of its attributes that it accepts is impossible. As for the impossibility of being free of all in the case of the created: it is because we know necessarily the impossibility of atoms being free of the kind of accidents (akwān); which are motion and rest, and conjunction and separation. So it must not be free of the other kinds of accidents that it accepts. As for in the case of the Eternal, Exalted and Glorified: it is because we know with certainty the impossibility of His being free of all the attributes that His act indicates; of knowledge, power, will, and life. For if these attributes were negated with respect to Him, it would be impossible for Him to bring into existence any of His acts, and then the non-existence of all created things would follow, despite their existence being actual, and that is impossible necessarily. And when it is impossible for Him to be free of these attributes, then it necessarily follows that it is impossible for Him to be free of the other attributes that He accepts; because of what you have known of the necessity of the equality of the relationship of the accepted to the essence that is receptive to them. And when the concomitance between the existence of His Essence, Exalted is He, and all His attributes by which He is qualified is established... then it necessarily follows that all of them are eternal. For if any of them were created, given the assumption that He cannot be free of any of His attributes... then it would require that the existence of His Essence be created, but being created of His Essence is impossible because of what you know of the necessity of His pre-eternity. So the supposition of createdness in any of His attributes is impossible.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage contains the main proof that if acceptance is essential, the essence cannot be devoid of any attribute it accepts. Sanusi argues: since the relationship of the essence to all its accepted attributes is equal, if it were possible to lack all of them, then it could lack any, but that is impossible. He then applies this to two cases: contingent beings (الحادث) and the Eternal (القديم). For contingent beings, we know necessarily that atoms cannot be free of the genus of accidents (الأكوان) like motion and rest, so they cannot be free of other accidents. For God, we know that He must have those attributes indicated by His acts: knowledge, power, will, life. If He were free of these, He could not act, which is impossible. Then, since acceptance is equal, He cannot be free of any other attribute He accepts. Finally, he concludes that because God's existence is eternal and He cannot be without these attributes, all His attributes are necessarily eternal. If any attribute were created, then God's essence would become created—impossible. Therefore, all attributes are eternal.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God could have some attributes but not others, e.g., He could be powerful but not knowledgeable.
Correction: Sanusi proves that if acceptance is essential, God cannot lack any attribute He accepts. Since His acts indicate He accepts certain attributes (knowledge, power, etc.), He must accept all, and thus cannot lack any.

Checkpoint

A) Because they are all created.
B) Because God could not have them without being created.
C) Because the essence is eternal and cannot lack any attribute, so they must all be eternal.
D) Because the attributes are the same as the essence.

Key Takeaway
The essential acceptance of attributes means an essence cannot be devoid of any accepted attribute, and for God this entails the eternity of all His attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

You just learned that God cannot lack any attribute. He is necessarily All-Knowing, All-Powerful, All-Willing. Do you truly live as if He knows every thought in your mind? If He does, and He never changes, how will you change what you think or do today?
?
This passage says that if God lacked any attribute, He could not act – and you would not exist. Your very being depends on His eternal attributes. How does that truth move you to gratitude? What will you thank Him for specifically right now?
?
Sanusi proves that God's attributes are eternal and inseparable from His essence. Does your heart sometimes imagine that God 'grows' or 'changes' in His knowledge or mercy? If you really believe He has always been exactly as He is – full of knowledge and power – does that make you fear Him more or trust Him more? What would change in your actions today if you lived with that certainty?

Objection and Answer: God's Attributes Are Essential, Not Merely Temporal
Sanusi presents and answers an objection regarding the proof for God's eternal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi answers the objection that the proof from God's actions only proves temporal necessity for His attributes, not essential necessity.

Core Idea
The act proves temporal necessity, but divine attributes are essential, not just temporal.

This passage tackles a subtle objection: doesn't the argument from God's creation only show He has attributes at the moment of creation, not eternally? Sanusi carefully distinguishes between temporal necessity (proved by the act) and absolute essential necessity (which is the actual claim). Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the Islamic doctrine of eternal attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Look for the sentence that presents the objection: the proof from God's act only shows temporal necessity.
The objection is that the act only proves attributes at the time of the act, not forever.
2
Distinguish temporal from essential necessity
Focus on Sanusi's distinction between wujūb waqtī (temporal necessity) and wujūb muṭlaq (absolute necessity). Understand that temporal necessity is more general, and essential necessity is more specific.
Use the examples given in the commentary to solidify the difference.
3
Understand why the objection fails
Sanusi argues that the implication of the more general (temporal) does not entail the implication of the more specific (essential). So the proof from the act only gives temporal necessity, not the essential necessity that would make the attributes eternal.
This is a key logical move in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولو فُرِضَتْ حادثةً لَلزِمَ الدورُ أو التسلسل ؛ لتوقفِ إحداثها عليها ) هذا جواب عن سؤال استشعرْتُ ورودَهُ ، وتقريرُهُ أَنْ يُقالَ : ما ذكرتُم في حقِّ الحادثِ مِن استحالة عرو الجواهر عن بعض ما تقبلُهُ - وهو الأكوان - فيلزم ألا تعرى عن سائر ما تقبله .. مُسلَّم ؛ لأنَّ استحالة عروها عن الأكوانِ معلوم بالضرورة ، وأما ما ذكرتُم في حقِّ القديمِ مِنِ استحالةِ عروهِ تعالى عن العلم والقدرة والإرادة والحياة فيلزم استحالة عروه عن سائر ما يقبلُهُ مِنَ الصفاتِ .. قد لا يُسلَّم لكم
القولُ باستحالة عروه عن الأوصاف المذكورة حتى يتم لكم استدلالكم بها على استحالة عروه عن سائر صفاتِهِ
قولكم في دليل استحالة عروه عن الأوصاف المذكورة : ( إِنَّ فعلهُ الموجود دلَّ عليها مِنْ حيثُ توقف إيجادِهِ الاختياري على اتصافه بتلك الصفاتِ المذكورة ) ، نقولُ : إنَّما يدلُّ الفعلُ على وجوب اتصافِ فاعله بتلك الصفاتِ وجوباً وقتيّاً ؛ أعني : وقت إيجادِهِ ذلكَ الفعل . لا وجوباً مطلقاً بحسَبِ الذاتِ ، والذي يُوجِبُ استحالة العرو.. الثاني لا الأوَّلُ (۱) ؛ لما عُلِمَ أنَّ الوقتيَّة المطلقة أعمُّ مِنَ الضروريَّةِ المطلقة ، وملزوم الأعم غير ملزوم الأخص (۲)
والحاصلُ : أَنَّ الذي أنتجه دليلكم أعمُّ مِنْ مدَّعاكم (۳)
(۱) قوله : ( الثاني ( خبر الاسم الموصول ، وهذا الثاني هو وجوب اتصاف الذات بصفاتها التي ثبتت بالعقل مطلقاً ، وقوله : ( لا الأوَّلُ ) هو اتصافها بهذه الصفات فقط عند الإيجاد
(۲) الوقتية المطلقة : هي القضية التي يجب محمولها لموضوعها في وقت معين من غير تقييد بعدم الدوام عند مفارقة الوقت ؛ كقولنا : كل إنسان متحرك الأصابع وقت الكتابة ، والضرورية المطلقة : هي التي يجب محمولها لموضوعها ما دامت ذاته ؛ إذ كلما وجب المحمول للموضوع بحسب الذات وجب بحسب الوقت ولا عكس ، فيصدقان معاً في قولنا : كل إنسان حيوان ؛ تصدق ضرورية مطلقة بأن تقول : كل إنسان حيوان بالضرورة وقت كونه إنساناً . مفاد عكاري » ( ق ۱۸۸ )
(۳) قوله : ( دليلكم ) هو إيجاد الفعل ، وقوله : ( أعم من مدَّعاكم ) أي : لأنَّ الدليل أنتج الوجوب الوقتي للصفات ، وهو أعم من وجوبها بحسب الذات الذي هو المدعى . « حامدي » ( ص ٢٥٦ )
His saying: (And if it were assumed to be temporally originated, then circularity or infinite regress would be entailed, because its bringing into existence depends on them) This is an answer to a question that I sensed would arise. Its explication is that it may be said: What you mentioned regarding the temporally originated [realm]—the impossibility of the substances being devoid of some of what they receive—which is the accidents (akwān)—so that they must not be devoid of the rest of what they receive—is granted; because the impossibility of their being devoid of accidents is known necessarily. But what you mentioned regarding the Eternal—the impossibility of His being devoid, exalted, of knowledge, power, will, and life—so that the impossibility of His being devoid of the rest of the attributes He receives follows—may not be granted to you—The statement that the impossibility of His being devoid of the mentioned attributes is granted only if your inference from them to the impossibility of His being devoid of His other attributes is completed. Your proof for the impossibility of His being devoid of the mentioned attributes: (Verily His existing act indicates them because His voluntary bringing into existence depends on His being qualified with those mentioned attributes). We say: The act only indicates the necessity of the agent being qualified with those attributes with a temporal necessity; I mean: at the time of His bringing into existence that act. Not with an absolute necessity in terms of the essence. And what necessitates the impossibility of being devoid is the second, not the first; because it is known that absolute temporal [necessity] is more general than absolute essential [necessity], and the implication of the more general is not the implication of the more specific. The summary: that what your proof produced is more general than your claim. (1) His saying: (the second) is the predicate of the relative pronoun, and this second is the necessity of the essence being qualified with its attributes that are established by reason absolutely; and His saying: (not the first) is its being qualified with these attributes only at the time of bringing into existence. (2) Absolute temporal [necessity] is the proposition whose predicate is necessary for its subject at a specific time without being restricted to non-continuity when the time passes; like our saying: every human moves his fingers at the time of writing. And absolute essential [necessity] is that whose predicate is necessary for its subject as long as its essence exists; since whenever the predicate is necessary for the subject by essence, it is necessary by time but not vice versa. They both hold true together in our saying: every human is an animal; it is true as an absolute essential [proposition] that you say: every human is an animal by necessity at the time he is human. (3) His saying: (your proof) is the bringing into existence of the act; and His saying: (more general than your claim) means: because the proof produced temporal necessity for the attributes, and that is more general than their necessity by essence, which is the claim.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and answer. First, Sanusi introduces an anticipated question: an opponent might challenge the application of the principle to God. The objection is: You (the theologians) grant that in the physical world (al-ḥādith), substances cannot be devoid of accidents (akwān) like motion and rest, and from this you infer they must have all accidents. That much is admitted because it is known necessarily. But when you apply the same reasoning to God, claiming that because He cannot be devoid of attributes like knowledge, power, will, and life (which are proven from His act), He must also have every possible attribute, that may not be accepted. The objector then specifies: the proof that God cannot be devoid of those four attributes is based on the argument from the act (fi‘l): God's voluntary creation requires that He possess these attributes at the moment of creation. The answer (given by Sanusi) is that the act only proves the necessity of these attributes at the time of the act—a temporal necessity (wujūb waqtī). It does not prove an absolute necessity (wujūb muṭlaq) inherent to the essence. The impossibility of being devoid of attributes (which would prove they are essential) requires the second type, not the first. Why? Because absolute temporal necessity is more general (a‘amm) than absolute essential necessity (ḍarūriyya muṭlaqa). Whatever is essential is also temporal, but not vice versa. The implication of the more general (the temporal) does not entail the implication of the more specific (the essential). So the proof from the act only establishes a general temporal necessity, not the specific claim of essential necessity. Sanusi then summarizes: what the opponent's proof yields is more general (a‘amm) than what they claim (the essential necessity). The three footnotes clarify: (1) The difference between 'the second' (absolute essential necessity) and 'the first' (temporal necessity). (2) Definitions of absolute temporal and absolute essential propositions with examples. (3) Confirmation that the act only proves temporal necessity, which is more general than the claimed essential necessity.

وجوب مطلق
ضرورية مطلقة
وقتية مطلقة
الدور
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof from God's act proves that God's attributes are essential (always present).
Correction: The act only proves temporal necessity (attributes at the time of creation), not essential necessity.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's answer, what kind of necessity for God's attributes does the argument from the act prove?
A) Absolute essential necessity.
B) Temporal necessity at the time of the act.
C) Necessity by divine decree.
D) Necessity by human reason.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi shows that the argument from creation only establishes temporal necessity for God's attributes, not the essential necessity that would make them eternal; but the actual doctrine of attributes rests on a different proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever subtly reduce God's attributes to being relevant only when they affect your life—His knowledge only when you need guidance, His power only when you need help? How does the distinction between temporal and essential necessity challenge you to see God's attributes as eternally existing, independent of your circumstances? What would change in your worship if you truly believed that God's attributes are essential and not just reactive to creation?
?
The objection in this lesson arises from applying the logic of temporal creation to the Eternal. In your own heart, do you sometimes project human limitations onto God—expecting Him to act like a human, to change His mind, or to be constrained by time? How does this lesson call you to repent of such projections and to adore God as utterly transcendent?
?
Sanusi argues that the act only proves temporal necessity, not essential. Consider your own acts of obedience: do you sometimes perform them only to get a temporal result, or do you see them as flowing from an eternal relationship with God? Are your good deeds merely 'temporal' or are they rooted in an essential commitment to God? How can you shift from temporal obedience to essential devotion?

Sanusi's Reductio: Actions Indicate Absolute Necessity
Sanusi answers an objection and proves actions indicate absolute necessity via reductio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that actions only prove temporal necessity fails, and how Sanusi uses a reductio argument (infinite regress) to establish the absolute necessity of God's attributes.

Core Idea
If God's attributes were merely possible, they'd be contingent—and that leads to an infinite chain.

In this passage, Sanusi confronts a serious objection: maybe actions only show that attributes are necessary for the moment of creation, not eternally. He replies with a powerful argument: if attributes were possible, they would be contingent, and their existence would require yet more attributes, leading to circularity or infinite regress. This shows that actions must point to absolute, eternal necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objector claims that actions only prove the necessity of attributes at the time of action (temporal necessity), not an eternal absolute necessity. Understand the challenge.
The objection is stated indirectly in the passage as something Sanusi denies.
2
Follow Sanusi's reductio
If the attributes were merely possible (jā'iz), they would be contingent (ḥādith). Then the agent would need similar attributes to produce them, leading to an infinite chain of attributes. Notice how each step forces a new attribute.
The argument uses the principle that every possible is originated.
3
Recognize the dilemma
If the second set of attributes is the same as the first, circularity (dawr) results. If different, infinite regress (tasalsul) results. Both are impossible, so the original attributes cannot be possible.
This is the core of the reductio ad absurdum.
4
Understand the counter-objection and reply
A second objection claims that Sanusi's argument is not a direct inference from the action but a separate proof. Sanusi replies that it is indeed a valid inference because the possibility of attributes leads to impossibility, so the action implies necessity.
Sanusi concludes that the action indicates absolute necessity, and the mention of circularity/regress explains the manner of that indication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جوابه : منعُ أَنَّ الأفعالَ إِنَّما دلَّتْ على وجوبِ تلك الصفات لفاعلها وجوباً وقتيّاً ، بل وجوباً مطلقاً بحسَبِ الذاتِ ، بحيثُ يستحيلُ [؟] تلك الصفات مطلقاً [؟] عرو الفاعل عن [؟] وبيانُ ذلكَ : أنَّهُ لو قُدِّرَ الجواز لتلك الصفاتِ لكانَتْ مِنْ جملة الأفعال الحادثة ؛ ضرورةَ أنَّ كلَّ ممكن حادث ، فيجب أن يتّصفَ فاعلُها بأمثالها ؛ ليتمكَّنَ بها مِنْ إيجادها ، ثم ننقل الكلام إلى تلكَ الصفاتِ الأُخر ، فإنْ قُدْرَ لها الجواز أيضاً لزم حدوثها أيضاً ، ولزم اتصافُ فاعلها بأمثالها ؛ ليتمكَّنَ بها أيضاً مِنْ إيجادِها ، ولزم الدورُ إِنْ كانَتْ هذه الصفاتُ هي الأولى ، أو التسلسل إنْ كانَتْ غيرَها ! فإذاً ؛ الأفعالُ لا يمكن صدورها عن فاعل تكون تلك الصفاتُ في حقه جائزة لا يُقالُ : نحنُ إنَّما اعترضنا على استدلالكم على وجوبها بمجرَّدِ الفعل ، وهذا الذي أجبتُم بهِ لم يصح الاستدلال بهِ على ذلك ، بل حاصله : استنباط دليل آخر على وجوبِ تلك الصفاتِ للفاعل ؛ وهو أنَّها لو كانَتْ جائزةً للزمَ الدورُ أو التسلسل ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : إِنَّما استلزم جواز تلك الصفاتِ الدور أو التسلسل من حيثُ إِنَّ كلَّ جائز لا يكون إلا فعلاً حادثاً ، والفعلُ الحادث يدلُّ على تلك الصفاتِ ، ثم ننقل الكلام إليها ، ويلزم الدورُ أو التسلسل . فصح إذاً : أنَّ الفعل يدلُّ على وجوب تلك الصفاتِ وجوباً مطلقاً بحسَبِ الذاتِ ، وذكرُ الدورِ والتسلسل في هذا الجواب بيان لوجهِ دلالتِهِ على ذلك ، والله الموفق . وقوله : ( لتوقف إحداثها عليها ) أي : على أمثالها
His answer: denial that actions only indicate the necessity of those attributes for their agent in a temporal necessity, but rather an absolute necessity according to the essence, such that it is impossible [??] those attributes absolutely [??] the agent being free from [??] and its explanation is that: if possibility were supposed for those attributes, they would be among the contingent actions; necessarily every contingent is originated, so their agent must be described by their likes in order to be able to produce them. Then we transfer the discussion to those other attributes, if possibility is supposed for them as well, then their origination also follows, and the agent's being described by their likes also follows in order to be able to produce them. And circularity would follow if these attributes are the first, or infinite regress if they are others! So then actions cannot issue from an agent for whom those attributes are possible. It cannot be said: We only objected to your inference of their necessity by mere action, and this which you have answered with is not valid as an inference upon that, but rather its outcome is the derivation of another proof for the necessity of those attributes for the agent; namely that if they were possible, circularity or infinite regress would follow. For we say: The possibility of those attributes necessitated circularity or infinite regress only because every possible is nothing but a contingent action, and the contingent action indicates those attributes, then we transfer the discussion to them, and circularity or infinite regress follows. So it is established then that the action indicates the necessity of those attributes with absolute necessity according to the essence, and the mention of circularity and infinite regress in this answer is an explanation of the aspect of its indication upon that. And God is the Grantor of success. And his saying: (because the production of them depends on them) i.e., on their likes.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The author first states the objection: critics claim that actions only prove a temporal necessity for the attributes (wujūban waqtiyyan), not an eternal necessity (wujūban muṭlaqan). The answer begins by showing the consequence if the attributes were merely possible (jā'iz). If they were possible, they would be contingent (ḥādith) like all possible things. Then the agent would need similar attributes to produce them, leading to an infinite chain. If those attributes are also possible, the same reasoning applies, and you get either circularity (dawr) if they are the same, or infinite regress (tasalsul) if different. Thus actions cannot proceed from an agent whose attributes are merely possible—they must be necessary. A counter-objection follows: the opponent says this is not a direct inference from the action itself but a separate argument. The author replies that the inference is valid because the mere possibility of the attributes would lead to impossibility (dawr or tasalsul), so by reductio the attributes are necessary. The conclusion is that action indeed indicates absolute necessity of the attributes. The final note explains a phrase from the text: 'because the production of them depends on them' meaning the production of contingent actions depends on attributes similar to them.

وجوباً مطلقاً
الدور
التسلسل
الجواز
الحادث
الفعل
الصفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that actions only prove the necessity of attributes at the time of creation, not eternally.
Correction: Sanusi shows that if attributes were merely possible, they would be contingent and lead to circularity or infinite regress, which is impossible. Therefore, actions prove absolute eternal necessity.

Checkpoint
What consequence follows if the attributes of God were merely possible (jā'iz)?
A) They could be known through revelation alone.
B) They would be contingent and lead to circularity or infinite regress.
C) They would be eternal like the essence.
D) They would be unnecessary for creation.

Key Takeaway
The action indicates the absolute necessity of God's attributes, because their possibility would lead to an impossible chain of circularity or infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's attributes could ever be possible rather than necessary, would that change your confidence in His promises? Do you ever act as though God might not keep His word? What would it mean to truly live today knowing that His attributes are absolutely necessary? Commit to one situation this week where you will trust His absolute perfection.
?
Sanusi's argument shows that even a hint of possibility in God's attributes leads to absurdity. Where in your heart have you allowed a 'maybe' about God's power, knowledge, or justice? Are there areas where you doubt His perfection? Repent of that and ask Him to strengthen your certainty.
?
The reductio forces you to choose: either God's attributes are absolutely necessary or the universe makes no sense. Have you ever acted as if God's attributes are optional—treating His commands as suggestions? How would your daily decisions change if you fully internalized that His attributes are necessary and unchanging? Write down one practical change you will make from today.

Impossibility of Non-Existence and Change for the Eternal
Sanusi establishes the impossibility of non-existence and change for the eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the eternal essence and attributes of Allah are absolutely immutable and cannot cease to exist.

Core Idea
Eternity entails absolute immutability and impossibility of non-existence.

Sanusi now draws a critical conclusion from the previous discussions on the eternity of attributes. He establishes a universal principle: whatever is proven eternal cannot cease to exist. He then applies this to both the essence and attributes of Allah, showing that they are entirely free from change. This lesson grounds the doctrine of divine immutability in rational necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author moves from a general principle to specific applications.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the universal principle
Find the sentence that states the universal rule: 'كل ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه'. Understand that this is the foundation for the rest.
3
Distinguish the two applications
The passage then applies the principle to two cases: the essence and the attributes. Notice the different reasons given for each.
For the essence: due to its eternity and permanence. For the attributes: due to what was mentioned about their eternity.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends by stating that change is absolutely impossible for the Eternal. Ask yourself why this is a necessary conclusion.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما وجب قدمه استحال عدمُهُ . وإذا عرفتَ وجوب قدم الصفاتِ عرفت استحالة عدمها ؛ لما قدَّمنا مِنْ بيانِ استحالة العدم على القديم. هذا ظاهر ، وقد قدمنا برهان القاعدة الكليَّةِ ؛ وهي أنَّ كلَّ ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه . ذات القديم وصفاته لا تقبل التغير مطلقاً . فخرج لك بهذا استحالة التغير على القديم مطلقاً. أما في ذاتِهِ : فلوجوب قدمِهِ وبقائِهِ ؛ لما مرَّ . وأما في صفاتِهِ : فلما ذُكِرَ الآنَ ، ومِنْ ثَمَّ استحال
What has been proven eternal, its non-existence is impossible. And if you have known the necessity of the eternity of the attributes, you have known the impossibility of their non-existence, based on what we have presented of the explanation of the impossibility of non-existence for the eternal. This is apparent, and we have presented the proof of the universal principle, which is that everything whose eternity is established, its non-existence is impossible. The essence of the Eternal and His attributes do not accept change absolutely. So there follows for you from this the impossibility of change for the Eternal absolutely. As for His essence: due to the necessity of its eternity and permanence, as has passed. As for His attributes: due to what has been mentioned now, and therefore it is impossible.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal conclusion and classification. The author first states the principle: whatever is proven to be eternal (qadīm) cannot cease to exist—its non-existence is impossible. This is applied to the divine attributes: since the attributes are eternal, they cannot perish. Then a universal rule is given: everything whose eternity is established is impossible to be non-existent. Next, the author asserts that both the essence (dhāt) and attributes (ṣifāt) of the Eternal (al-Qadīm) do not admit change (taghayyur) at all. The reason for the essence is its necessary eternity and permanence (baqā'), as previously proven. For the attributes, it follows from the same proofs of their eternity and the impossibility of non-existence discussed. The passage concludes that change is absolutely impossible for the Eternal, both in essence and attributes.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the attributes, though eternal, could change or cease.
Correction: This passage establishes that eternity entails absolute immutability and impossibility of non-existence for both the essence and attributes.

Key Takeaway
The eternal essence and attributes of Allah are absolutely immutable and cannot cease to exist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

When you doubt His mercy because of a hardship, do you truly believe that His mercy is eternally fixed, or are you measuring Him by your changing circumstances? What would it mean for you today to trust in a mercy that never wavers?
?
Your own character changes with moods, health, and time. Compare that to Allah's immutable attributes. Is there an attribute of Allah—like His justice or His patience with your sins—that you have assumed might change based on your recent failings? How does this lesson demand you recalibrate your confidence in Him?
?
The passage teaches that non-existence is impossible for Allah. Yet you exist only because He wills it. Are you living as if your own existence depends entirely on His permanence, or do you act as if you are self-sufficient? What would change in your prayer today if you truly felt that you could vanish if He withdrew His eternal act of sustaining you?
